The Urgency of Wuxi's Relief for the Silk Industry 116

The Ministry of Industry believes that the silk of Jiangsu and Zhejiang is a major part of foreign trade. In recent years, due to farmers adhering to the status quo and silk merchants and reelers failing to improve, production has lagged behind. At the same time, it has also been affected by the dumping of Japanese silk, causing silk factories to fail year after year. In order to actively improve, it has repeatedly ordered the directors of the industrial departments of the two provinces to negotiate relief measures in Shanghai. Director He of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Industry believes that the silk industry in Jiangsu is centered on Wuxi. He specially came to Wuxi to invite various industries related to banking, money, silk, and silkworms to discuss seriously. However, due to the lack of cash, all parties felt difficult. However, the spring cocoons will be on the market in an instant. If measures are not taken early, tens of millions of natural products will inevitably be completely destroyed. It was decided to dry them on behalf of others, calculating the dry cocoon production in the province at 70,000 loads, which requires about 540,000 yuan for drying. The government subsidizes half of it, and the other half is raised by the cocoon-producing counties themselves. The "Wuxi Silk Area Relief Committee" has been established, and local groups and various industries related to banking, money, silk, and silkworms are working together to send a telegram to the provincial government and the Department of Industry, asking for subsidies. Because the provincial treasury is empty, it cannot be subsidized. It was decided to temporarily allow the allocation of debt vouchers, which must be returned within a time limit. The Silk Area Relief Committee was immediately replied to by telegram. After receiving the telegram, the relief committee believed that if the provincial government had no cash subsidies, then all measures could not proceed. Yesterday, it sent another telegram to the Department of Industry, stating that "drying on behalf of others is originally to protect natural products and relieve agricultural famine. If we talk about local commerce, it happens to be after the Shanghai war and the failure of the silk industry last year. The end of May is approaching, all industries are bleak, and the cocoon market is depressed. There is a lack of cash in the mainland. Banking, money, silk, and cocoons all feel difficult. Whether or not drying on behalf of others can be done depends entirely on whether there are funds from the province. We sincerely ask the provincial government to try its best to find a way to allocate cash subsidies. Wuxi plans to purchase 80,000 loads of cocoons this year, and the drying cost per load is 2.67 yuan. A subsidy of half requires about 100,000 yuan, so the financial aspects can gradually collect and borrow half of it to help make things happen," etc. The directors of various banks in Jiangyin jointly entered the province on the 19th to ask the provincial government to consider the plight of farmers and the pity of natural products being destroyed. The cash subsidy must also assist in debt vouchers of 500,000 yuan at the minimum, which is difficult to return within a time limit. The silk factory colleagues also convened a general meeting yesterday. According to the principle that Director He showed "strictly prohibiting speculative improvement work", they seriously discussed and decided that factories that can meet this principle must register with the association before June 15th. All the expenses during the drying period will also be shared equally according to the number of vehicles.

Zhenjiang Provincial Capital Begins Trial of Public Buses 117

Many trunk roads in Jiangsu Province have been built. Zhenrong and other three commercial bus companies have too few vehicles and expensive fares, and there are few passengers. In order to popularize civilian travel, the Jiangsu Construction Department is conducting a trial of public buses. The preparations have now been completed, and it is scheduled to start operating today (21st). It is divided into three routes: the first route is from Jinshan River Estuary to Huashang Wharf, the second route is from the Education Department to Jinshan River Estuary, and the third route is from Nanmen Station to Huashang Wharf. The second and third routes are being tried first. It is said that the full fare for each route is only 56 copper coins.

Education News

Important News

Drafted by Jiangsu Department of Education 127

Three-Year Education Plan (II)

7. Improve Vocational Education

To improve vocational education, the following items should be implemented during this period:

(A) Enrich equipment, add practice fields, and establish connections with various industrial organizations to supplement the inadequacy of school equipment.

(B) Strictly enroll students. Vocational talents should be carefully selected, preferring quality over quantity, to eliminate the chronic problem of class sizes being filled superficially.

(C) Prepare to restore the Provincial Suzhou Industrial School. The original school buildings and machinery of the Jiangsu Provincial Industrial Specialized School have been abandoned and unused. Therefore, within the feasible scope of funding during this period, preparations should be made to restore the Suzhou Industrial School, temporarily offering high school civil engineering and dyeing and weaving departments. Graduates of junior high schools with excellent grades and a desire to dedicate themselves to the industrial sector should be selected to study for three years. In collaboration with the Department of Industry, a special weaving and finishing workshop should be established in the dyeing and weaving department, organized and managed according to industrial economic principles. Students of the dyeing and weaving department must be managed by the workshop when they enter the workshop for practice and are no different from the workers in the workshop.

8. Organize General Middle Schools. The organization of general middle schools is divided into the following items:

(A) Restrict county-run high schools. The funding and equipment for high schools are beyond the economic capacity of a single county at present. Therefore, for each county that has already established a high school, its actual funding amount and equipment status should be strictly examined. Those with confirmed funding and adequate equipment should be approved or denied for continued operation separately.

(B) Enforce the full-time system for middle school teachers. In Jiangsu Province, most middle school teachers are actually based on a time-based system, where their responsibility ends after completing their teaching. In the future, the full-time system should be enforced to achieve a consistent understanding between teachers and students and the effect of personality influence, which can also help rectify the academic atmosphere and discipline.

(C) Implement the trial examination and investigation system for all levels of middle school. To improve the academic ability of middle school students and eliminate the malpractice of teachers and students being perfunctory, the trial examination and investigation system for all levels should be implemented.

9. Improve the Efficiency of Social Education

(A) Strictly assess social education personnel.

(B) Determine the standard of treatment for social education personnel at all levels.

(C) Eliminate the waste of social education institutions.

(D) Actively carry out literacy campaigns.

(E) Complete the establishment of the Provincial Zhenjiang Library within this period.

Years Two and Three: Expansion Period 128

Items that have not been completed in the first year of organization should still be actively carried out during this period. The expansion that should be carried out during this period includes compulsory education, normal education, vocational education, and social education.

1. Increase Funding

(A) Establish county clearing houses and committees to increase educational funding. (B) Investigate and recover the assets of abandoned temples and recover publicly owned assets that have been privately occupied. (C) Award generous prizes for donating to establish schools. (D) Increase the income of the provincial educational forests.

2. Actively Expand Primary School Education

(A) Increase the number of primary schools. During the organizational period in the first year, increasing the number of grades and student quotas can increase the number of enrolled children by 137,560. Counting the original number of enrolled children of 580,820, there are a total of more than 710,000 enrolled children. However, there are still approximately 3,995,296 out-of-school children in the province. According to the National Education Conference plan, which stipulates universal compulsory education within 20 years, the number of out-of-school children should be reduced by 5% each year, which is an increase of 200,000 enrolled children. Therefore, starting from the 22nd year, the province should increase the number of primary schools by 4,000 grades (50 students per grade), with a cost of 250 yuan per grade, requiring a total of 1 million yuan per year. In addition, the newly added primary schools should use temples and other public assets as school sites, with an opening cost of approximately 150 yuan per grade, requiring a total of 600,000 yuan. The total cost of recurring expenses and opening costs in the 22nd year is 1.6 million yuan. This large sum seems daunting at first glance, but if the county's funding and school assets are actively cleared and all malpractices are eliminated, it will not be difficult to raise this funding. If it is indeed difficult to raise sufficient funding and the number of schools cannot be increased as planned, then actively improving private schools to accommodate school-age children can also supplement the inadequacy of primary schools.

(B) Jointly increase the number of complete primary schools.

(C) Increase vocational subjects and practice fields in higher primary schools.

(D) Promote the central primary school district system.

3. Expand Normal Education

(A) Complete the independence of normal middle schools throughout the province. The independence of normal middle schools throughout the province should be completed within the next two years and their equipment should be supplemented to an appropriate level.

(B) Enrich the content of rural normal schools. Within the next two years, the physics and chemistry equipment of all rural normal schools in the province should be supplemented to an appropriate level. Starting from the 22nd year, a rural high school normal department should be added to each rural normal school, selecting junior high school graduates with excellent grades who are willing to serve in rural primary schools to study for two years. (C) Increase the departments of provincial normal colleges. During this period, in addition to the original literature, history, and geography departments, mathematics, physics, and chemistry departments should be added, and the equipment of each department should be actively completed.

(D) Increase the number of normal schools to prepare for compulsory education teachers. According to the investigation, only over 1,600 normal school graduates graduate each year in this province. Even if all of them serve in primary schools, it is not enough. Moreover, most of them go on to higher education or change to other jobs. During this period, the number of primary school grades must increase by 4,000 grades each year, which means that 4,000 more normal school graduates should be added each year, calculated at 50 students per class. 80 more classes of normal school students should be added each year. However, since the 21st year is the organization period and funding is also difficult, it has been changed to be added starting from the 22nd year. During this period, if there are not enough teachers, qualified personnel who have passed the primary school teacher certification can be appointed. It is estimated that starting from the 22nd year, 80 more classes of normal school students will be added each year, with a recurring cost of approximately 50 yuan per class including food expenses, totaling 400,000 yuan. If half of the classes are added to existing normal schools, the equipment cost will be increased by 500 yuan per class, with 40 classes requiring 20,000 yuan. For the remaining 40 classes, the opening cost will be 20,000 yuan per school, divided among ten schools, requiring a total of 200,000 yuan. The total cost of implementing this plan is approximately 620,000 yuan. This funding can be paid from the increased revenue from reorganizing the provincial funding tax sources. However, to ensure the funding is reliable, this plan will be implemented in phases over two years.

(E) Implement the graduation association system for normal middle schools throughout the province.

(F) Hold summer workshops.

4. Expand the Content of Vocational Education

(A) Supplement all the necessary equipment inside and outside the schools of agricultural, sericultural, aquatic, and industrial vocational schools to an appropriate level, and expand fishing village normal schools.

(B) In response to the industrial environment, actively enrich the equipment of Suzhou Industrial School to pave the way for establishing specialized departments and, when necessary, prepare to establish other engineering departments.

(C) The practice fields established by various vocational schools must be managed in accordance with agricultural and industrial economic principles, and the results obtained must reach at least 80% of the original plan.

(D) During these two years, special attention should continue to be paid to integrating the vocational education undertakings that have already been carried out in the province with various industrial organizations run by businesses, provinces, and countries.

(E) Establish various simple vocational supplementary schools

5. Enrich the Content of General Middle Schools

(A) Supplement all the equipment of provincial middle schools that has not been enriched to a considerable level

(B) Implement the system of regional joint examinations for middle school graduates on a trial basis

(C) Implement the system of departmental inspection of middle schools

6. Continue to Actively Encourage Literacy Education

(A) In addition to running various undertakings, local social education institutions should continue to focus on encouraging literacy education. By the end of this period, the number of illiterate people should be reduced by 20%.

(B) Establish more public schools, open-air schools, forest schools, public night schools, and public literacy centers.

(C) Extend the graduation period of public schools appropriately, depending on the situation.

7. Increase the Number of Social Education Institutions

(A) Establish one provincial public education hall each in the former Huaiyang District and Susongtai District.

(B) Establish one provincial library each in suitable locations in Jiangnan and Jiangbei.

Recording of Knocking the Bell in the Old Temple (II) Not Removing the Weeds in the Courtyard by Zhaifu 135

(II)

The messenger of culture travels in China on a particularly slow train. Hải 亘史 invented the pendulum clock as early as 1656, but we have never bought a chiming clock in this old temple. No one in the village has ever seen this thing. In the past, everyone woke up in the morning to the crowing of the rooster, and started cooking dinner in the evening after watching the sunset. Since I took on the job of ringing the bell, it seems that everyone relies on me to report the time. I ring the bell three times a day... once in the morning, called the dawn bell; once at noon, called the noon bell. The villagers go to bed when they hear me ring the evening bell, get up when they hear me ring the dawn bell, and eat lunch when they hear me ring the noon bell. These have almost become the unwritten constitution of the villagers.

One day, I discovered a strange thing! Zhang Huzi in the village smokes opium according to the sound of the bell in the old temple. The evening bell awakens his sweet dreams, and he picks up his gun and indulges in opium. As soon as the dawn bell rings, he doesn't care about anything and lies on the bed with his limbs stretched out in the shape of the Chinese character for "sky", without moving. Taking off his clothes and covering himself with a quilt are all left to his young wife to take care of.

This was what Zhang's old mother, Shen Da's wife, told me when she came to the temple to burn incense. I then began to doubt my work. I questioned myself... "What is the meaning of ringing the bell? To wake someone up to smoke opium... to be the rooster of someone who smokes opium... does this deserve to be my life's work?" I doubted for many days, and once I almost went on strike. But time bleached away this doubt. I found out clearly that the majority of people who are woken up by me in the morning go to farm and work, and those who are woken up by me in the evening to smoke opium are only a small minority. Later, I made a new determination... Even if ringing this big bell only has the power to wake up one person to farm and work, I am still willing to continue ringing it until I am unable to ring it anymore.

(III)

In my hands, I hold the key to the work and rest of the entire village. Can I ring this big bell casually? If I am a little late today and a little early tomorrow, wouldn't that be a breach of trust? How can I ring this bell accurately? I am ringing the bell while racking my brains to find a solution.

The time of the noon bell is relatively easy to determine. I see the sun shining on people, and a black shadow falls on the ground. When the sun is in the east, the shadow falls in the west; when the sun is in the west, the shadow falls in the east; when the sun is in the south, the shadow falls in the north. When the sun rises, the shadow is infinitely long. After that, the sun gradually rises higher, and the shadow gradually becomes shorter, until the sun is at the top, and the shadow becomes the shortest. After this, the sun gradually lowers, and the shadow gradually lengthens again, until the sun sets and the shadow becomes infinitely long again. When the sun is at the top, the shadow shrinks from long to shortest and wants to lengthen from shortest, it is the local noon. At this time, the sun is in the due south, and the shadow is in the due north. Draw a line according to the shadow, which is the meridian, that is, the north-south line. I use this principle to take a straight bamboo pole and insert it straight into the ground. How to insert a bamboo pole straight? I learned this little skill from the bricklayer, Li Sibao, when he was building a wall. Anyone who is willing to observe the bricklayer building a wall will understand this principle. When the weather is clear, I wait for the pole shadow to be short and short, short to the point where it cannot be shorter and intentionally lengthens, and then I start ringing my noon bell. A bell rings, everyone is happy, and the whole village is preparing to enjoy their lunch... I was wrong again. Soon I discovered that there are many working people who have no lunch to eat. Hearing the noon bell but not being able to eat lunch, what kind of life is this? I would rather not ring this sad noon bell.

In Xi'an in Late August

The Chinese Science Society holds an annual meeting every autumn. This year will be the seventeenth annual meeting. Railway Bureau Prepares to Take Over North Station Tomorrow 140

There was talk that the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway would resume operations on the 20th, but it was delayed due to the Japanese army delaying its withdrawal. However, the section between Nanjing and Xiang has officially resumed operations. As for the Zhenru area, the Japanese army has scheduled to withdraw tomorrow morning (the 23rd). The Japanese army will also withdraw from the North Station on the afternoon of the same day. The Railway Bureau has received an order from the Ministry of Railways to send personnel to take over the North Station. In addition to the twelve railway police officers who entered the station to guard it the day before yesterday, more than ten laborers wearing symbols issued by the Japanese army were sent to the station yesterday (the 21st) to organize various miscellaneous items and clean the platforms. It is also understood that many craftsmen from the railway have been ordered to stay temporarily in the Huashang Hotel on Xinmin Road in Zhabei, waiting for the Japanese army to withdraw so that they can immediately enter the station to repair the station building, in order to fulfill the prediction of a trial run on the 25th and resuming operation on the 28th.

A telegram from Suzhou on the 21st stated that Chen Chengshi, the section chief of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, inspected Zhenru, Shanghai, and other stations on the 22nd. If there are no dangers along the way, passenger trains will be allowed to run on the 25th.

Method for Closing Accounts for the 20th Year 142

Mortgages and Long-Term Extensions, Interest Paid as Usual

War Zone Sends Letter to the Rehabilitation Committee to Handle

The Citizen's United Association, the General Federation of Commerce of All Roads, the French Concession Business Federation, and other three groups, each formed a restoration committee. Yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., the fifth committee meeting was held at the Citizen's United Association. Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Jiang Junyi, Qu Zhenhua, Li Weiliang, Zhang Xianfang, Wang Jian, She Hualong, Secretary Cao Zhigong, and others attended. Hu Fengxiang chaired the meeting, and Zhao Ziyun recorded the minutes. First, the chairman reported that the general closure of accounts for the 20th year would be implemented at the end of May this year. Various places have sent letters requesting the association to preside over the handling of the matter. How should this be handled? Please make a public decision. Everyone agreed that since the January 28th Incident in this port, all industries have embraced patriotic enthusiasm and stopped operations for two months, extending to April 1st. Although they reluctantly reopened for business, due to the losses from more than two months of closure and the lack of business after reopening, some were so deserted that they could hardly maintain a livelihood, let alone recover their business. It is impossible in reality to clear all accounts in the shortest possible period. It is not only that the general merchants and people feel great difficulties. After reviewing the letters from various places, they are all true. Relief should be provided to directly address the difficulties of the majority of merchants and indirectly remove the impossibility of the silver and money industries. As a result, the following was resolved: (1) Regarding the issue of closing accounts at the end of May: (A) Mortgages and long-term loans should continue to be extended, and interest should be paid as usual. (B) Loans to all households should be closed at the end of the year. (C) A letter should be sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to ask the silver and money industries to accommodate. (2) Regarding the issue of closing accounts in the war zone, a letter should be sent to the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee to handle it. Secretary Cao Zhigong was appointed to draft the letter.

A Bleeding Story of Collecting Donations 143

Collection Officer Actually Refuses Sight Drafts

Once an Example is Set, Taxpayers Lose Security

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession reported yesterday that a taxpayer, Gao Landan, was brutally beaten by a donation collector. A letter was sent to the Shanghai Municipal Council to negotiate: To Whom It May Concern: According to Gao Lanzhou's letter, nearly one million Chinese reside in the concession and have the obligation to pay taxes. The Shanghai Municipal Council sends people to collect taxes quarterly. When the donation collectors arrive at the residents' homes to collect taxes, their manner and prestige are beyond description in words. It is believed that your council members, who reside in the concession, must see these people four times a year with their prestigious manner. Lanzhou is a doctor who has resided in Shanghai for nearly twenty years. He currently resides at No. 76, the corner of Lloyd Road and Niuzhuang Road, and has established the Neutral Hospital for three years. Each time the Shanghai Municipal Council sends people with donation tickets to collect taxes from us, we pay promptly, fearing delays. On the morning of the 19th of this month, around 9 a.m., a certain Chinese man sent by the Shanghai Municipal Council entered the room with a fierce expression and the sound of boots. Lanzhou stood up to welcome him and politely asked if he could pay with a sight draft as he was running low on cash. Upon hearing this, the Chinese man responded with a thunderous voice, shaking his head, extending his waist, and waving his hand, saying "No, no, no." He repeated the two words and added, "Hurry, hurry." Lanzhou had no choice but to swallow his anger and politely negotiate. Who knew that the Chinese man would curse and turn around to leave, saying, "Go find money, I'll show you." A moment later, the Chinese man returned with another Chinese man and a Westerner. The original Chinese man was even more arrogant than before. He took out the donation ticket and demanded payment. Lanzhou said that a sight draft is no different from cash. If it is absolutely impossible to accommodate, please sit for a while while I borrow from friends and relatives. Before he could finish speaking, the Chinese man told the Westerner. The Westerner extended his evil palm and grabbed Lanzhou's throat and punched him in the mouth. The punch landed on the mouth, his tooth pierced his upper lip, and blood flowed down his face. The Chinese man kicked him repeatedly. His seventy-year-old mother heard the noise and came to the rescue, but was driven back by the Chinese man. The Westerner saw Lanzhou bleeding and realized that he had caused trouble. He ran out quickly, and the two Chinese men followed. Neighbors witnessed this and were angry but dared not speak. The carpenter can testify. This is all Lanzhou's personal experience. He humbly narrates this so that he can be vindicated. The issue of Lanzhou being insulted and injured is minor, but if this example is set, the Chinese residents of the concession will be in trouble. Advocating justice, and awaiting your decision, I will not say more. All the sales receipts from Renji Hospital have been kept at the Old Gate Police Station for verification. It is checked that the donation collector abused his power and injured people, which is detrimental to the Shanghai Municipal Council's discipline and infringes on the legal rights of residents. This trend should not be allowed to continue. According to the letter, it is appropriate to send a letter to you, hoping that you will investigate, quickly dismiss the three people, and pursue legal action.

Wang Zao Shi's Conversation 147

Wang Zao Shi, one of the strongest advocates for ending tutelage, made the following remarks to visitors yesterday: (Question) Is it possible to take the road of constitutionalism? Wang (Answer) At a time when foreign insults are pressing and people are living in poverty, I am extremely reluctant to see any more internal revolutions and conflicts. Therefore, in addition to lecturing, I have followed social figures in the hope of ending tutelage and implementing constitutionalism through peaceful means and a fighting spirit, to put politics on a normal track and avoid constant internal strife. However, whether this peaceful method will be effective depends on whether the ruling Kuomintang is aware of the situation. If the rule becomes increasingly dark and corrupt and refuses to return power to the people, it will inevitably lead to a great revolution and bloodshed. I observe the situation in all aspects of the country and the future trends of the world, and I fear that this kind of tragedy cannot be avoided. Our current call to end tutelage will be of no avail, but it is only to fulfill our duty and put our minds at ease. (Question) It is said that Mr. is an important figure in the National Socialist Youth Party, is that true? Wang (Answer) Now, anyone who criticizes the Kuomintang but is not like the Communist Party is suspected of being a national socialist from the Kuomintang's perspective. Therefore, the publications run by the Kuomintang even claim that the Shanghai University Professors' Association for National Salvation is controlled by national socialists, and point out that Xie Xunchu, Wu Zelin, Zhang Yi, Zhu Qinglai, and other gentlemen are all national socialists, which is not true. I am neither a Youth Party member, nor a Communist Party member, and certainly not a Kuomintang member. To this day, I still have no party affiliation. Kuomintang people often label people outside the party, which is tantamount to increasing the prestige of others and weakening their own morale, which is unwise. As for my personal active political views, I plan to publish a journal in the future to publish them one after another.

Representatives of the Southern Henan Relief Committee Hosted Shanghai Philanthropists Yesterday Noon 154

Report on the Disaster Situation in Southern Henan

The counties of Huangchuan, Guangshan, Gushi, Shangcheng, and other counties in southern Henan have long been occupied by the Red Bandits. After repeated suppressions, they have not been completely eliminated. The Henan party, government, and military authorities, in view of the lack of coordination, which gave the enemy an opportunity, specially divided the eight counties of Huangchuan, Guangshan, Gushi, Xishui, Shangcheng, Xinyang, Luoshan, and Zheng into a special zone to organize a Pacification Committee to coordinate party, government, military, suppression, and pacification. In the past three months, it has achieved considerable victories. However, since the local area suffered a flood last year, followed by the scourge of the Red Bandits and the rampant bandits, not only are ten houses empty, but there are no houses to be empty. The Pacification Committee is responsible for pacification but has no power to provide relief. Therefore, the committee sent committee member Yang Yifeng, and concurrently the magistrate of Huangchuan County and the commander of the 20th Route Guerrilla, Mei Zhichao, together with Li Huanying, a member of the Henan Relief Association, to Beijing and Shanghai to appeal. After arriving in Shanghai, they have been appealing to charitable organizations such as the Flood Relief Committee, the Flood Relief Emergency Relief Association, the Red Cross Society, the China General Relief Association, and the Sino-Foreign Relief Association, and to philanthropists such as Xu Jingren, Zhu Ziqiao, Wang Yiting, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Huang Jinrong, and Du Yuesheng. All charitable organizations and philanthropists have promised to do their best to help. In addition to the major philanthropists having already allocated 700 bags of rice for relief from the Red Cross's rice relief fund, they have also promised to do their best within the Flood Relief Committee. Yesterday at 12 noon, Li Huanying, Mei Zhichao, and Yang Yifeng hosted a banquet for the major philanthropists here at the Jue Lin Vegetarian Restaurant on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. More than a dozen guests came, including Xu Jingren, Wang Yiting, Qu Wenliu, and Li Xiaodong. After taking their seats, Yang Yifeng delivered a speech reporting on the suppression of the Red Bandits and the disaster situation in the special zone (the speech is omitted). Various photos of the disaster situation were also shown. The guests and hosts dispersed happily until 3 p.m.

The Shanghai Office of the Jiangsu Province War Zone Relief Committee received an official letter from the Qingpu County Government yesterday, stating that the Japanese army had completely withdrawn from the northeastern part of the county. Wine Merchants in Hongkou District Request Exemption from War-Time Liquor Tax 156

Letter to the Taxpayers' Association to Forward to the Shanghai Municipal Council for Negotiation

A letter from Lao Fulaie Company on Wuzhou Road to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association stated: "To Whom It May Concern: Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, the merchants and residents of our Hongkou District have borne the brunt. Although we have not suffered the tragedy of artillery fire, the killings and atrocities committed by the Japanese army in recent months are no different from a war zone. The residents have all evacuated, and the entire district has fallen into chaos. The market is depressed and has not yet recovered. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Council has taken the initiative to exempt us from the war-time patrol tax, which is greatly appreciated by the merchants and residents. Unexpectedly, we received a notice from the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating that the liquor licenses for the spring and summer seasons still require us to pay the tax, and instructed us to go to the council to collect the licenses within three days. Considering that in this Shanghai Incident, the Japanese army used the concession as a base, and the Shanghai Municipal Council did not take measures to stop it, causing the residents of the entire city to suffer great losses. During the war period, the entire Hongkou District was closed. The so-called liquor license for business is almost like waste paper. Therefore, it is only reasonable that our war-time liquor tax should be exempted in the same way as the patrol tax. How can it be an exception? Therefore, we ask your association to uphold justice and forward the request to the Shanghai Municipal Council for prompt negotiation, so as to achieve the goal of exemption, reduce losses, and maintain the difficulties of the merchants. This is our earnest prayer. Sincerely, the Old Fulaie Company on Wuzhou Road in Hongkou, May 21."

Zhejiang People Organize Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association 157

Office Established in the French Concession

The declaration of the Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association states: The Wenzhou-Chu salt region of Zhejiang Province was originally a tax-exempt area. After the seventh year of the Republic of China, the inspection offices were changed to tax collection at the salt production sites, allowing for free trade. The tax revenue began to flow smoothly. The annual regular tax revenue was between 600,000 and over 700,000 yuan. Officials and the people lived in peace, and the achievements were remarkable. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the Liangzhe Transportation Commissioner, due to a slight delay in revenue collection, rashly changed to commercial contracting. This practice has continued to this day, leading to numerous malpractices. It is said that there are those who govern people but lack governing methods, as the sages of the past discussed in detail. Initially, the slight delay in revenue collection was due to improper methods and lack of effort by the people. Therefore, after changing to commercial contracting, the deficit became even more severe. Contractors requested reductions in the contracted amount midway, sought to evade national taxes, and merchants and police committed murder and framed innocent people, leaving commoners with no avenue for appeal. Furthermore, merchants raised salt prices and fraudulently reported and embezzled funds. All kinds of evil phenomena became increasingly strange. Contractors monopolized the market, exploiting the common people, causing unbearable suffering. Salt officials colluded, preventing the grievances of the people from reaching the authorities. The members of this association are deeply concerned about this situation. Therefore, we gathered comrades to organize this association, aiming for the happiness of our homeland. We are determined to relieve the people from their suffering, feeling it is our undeniable responsibility. We held a meeting on May 17th and established the association. All elders and brothers of our two prefectures, regarding matters that should be promoted or reformed in salt administration, should send letters to this association at any time. We will compile them into proposals, discuss and decide upon them, and submit them to the Ministry of Finance and the Transportation Department for consideration. In case of any facts of officials and merchants harming the people, detailed evidence should be collected and sent to this association, which will forward it to the supervisory court for investigation, punishment of the wicked, and improvement according to the law, striving to provide support. In this way, the grievances of the people will not be blocked from reaching the authorities, and the malpractices can be reformed immediately, benefiting the people and the country. We hope that the elders and brothers of our two prefectures will share this responsibility with this association. Simple regulations of the Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association: (1) The purpose of this association is to improve salt affairs, benefit the people, and benefit the country. (2) The office is temporarily located at No. 9, Renhua Lane, Route Sapotille, French Concession, Shanghai. (3) This association has three standing committee members, seven executive committee members, three supervisory committee members, sixteen investigation committee members, an unspecified number of specialized committee members, one secretary, one accountant, one general affairs officer, and one editor. (4) Standing committee members, executive committee members, and supervisory committee members are elected by the general assembly. Investigation committee members and specialized committee members are appointed by the standing committee meeting. The secretary, accountant, general affairs officer, and editor are selected by the standing committee meeting. (5) Standing committee members, executive committee members, and supervisory committee members are elected from the members and serve a term of one year, with the possibility of re-election. Specialized committee members are appointed by the standing committee meeting from domestic salt administration experts with knowledge and experience, with no fixed term. (6) The general assembly is held once a year, and regular meetings are held quarterly. In case of urgent matters, the standing committee meeting may convene extraordinary meetings. (7) If standing committee members, executive committee members, or supervisory committee members are unable to attend due to circumstances, they may entrust a representative to attend. Specialized committee members may attend meetings to express their opinions, but they do not have voting rights. (8) Membership is limited to the people of the two prefectures. When joining the association, members must be introduced by at least two members of the association and approved by the committee. (9) The expenses of this association are raised by the members of the association. (10) This association may submit statements to the Ministry of Finance and Zhejiang Transportation Department at any time regarding the promotion and reform of salt administration and matters of officials and merchants harming the people, in order to express the grievances of the people. (11) This association is preparing to write and edit a monthly publication, which is managed by the editor. (12) These regulations shall take effect after being passed by the general assembly. List of officials appointed by the Wenzhou-Chu Salt Affairs Improvement Association: Standing Committee Members: Xiang Foshi, Chen Jingfu, Qian Zhifang; Executive Committee Members: Chen Jiansheng, Zhang Xingbai, Ye Yunhui, Zhao Chengzhi, Yin Yaofu, Wang Zhicheng, Ye Nanpo; Supervisory Committee Members: Xie Leiming, Dai Lifu, Chen Ziqin.

Laborer Picks Up a Bomb, Throws It, and Dies in Explosion 158

Zhabei War Zone has been undergoing organization, and the Commercial Press and Oriental Library on Baoshan Road have been hiring large numbers of laborers to clean up the remaining walls and broken rafters, busying themselves with post-war affairs. A laborer named Wu Da was working at the Oriental Library when he picked up a bomb in the ruins. He threw it to the ground, and it exploded with a loud bang. Wu Da was the first to be hit by the explosion and died on the spot. Three other companions were also injured: Xu Zhengwen, who was injured in the left hand and shoulder; Ding Zhongxiang, who was injured in both hands and whose life is in danger; and Zuo Shuan, who was injured in the right hand. The corpse was reported to the court for examination by the local security. The injured were rushed to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The deceased was from Jiangbei, 37 years old, and lived on East Broadway Road. He had a wife and several daughters. The aftermath is bleak. It is said that the company plans to provide generous compensation.

Young Man Brutally Murdered by Enemies 159

Eight Ax Wounds on His Body

Associated with the Underworld

Yesterday morning, the body of a young man who had been assassinated was found in a wheat field near the Siming Guild Hall west of Qichang Pier in Pudong. Cao Linhua, the local security of the sixteenth district, reported the incident to the local court, which dispatched a judge to the scene for examination at 4:00 PM. The deceased was about twenty years old, wearing a blue short shirt and trousers, with a leather belt around his waist. There were eight axe wounds on his right cheek, left forehead, top of the head, and back of the head, with blood and flesh blurred. About five or six feet to the left and right of the body, there were two large piles of bloodstains, as well as a duckbill cap and two black velvet shoes worn by the deceased, and several clumps of hair. It was evident that the deceased struggled fiercely with the murderer during the attack. The judge determined that the axe wounds were inflicted before death, causing fatal injuries. After the examination, as there were no relatives of the deceased, it was ordered that photographs be taken and the body placed in the hall for identification. According to the general public, the deceased was named Xiao A'nan, from Nanhui. He used to work as a carpenter in a shipyard in Lujiadu, Pudong. He had an elderly mother and younger brother. He was only twenty years old and not yet married. Recently, he abandoned his profession and associated with the underworld, relying on extortion to make a living. It is suspected that he was murdered by his accomplices.

Assassination of a Foreman 160

Gao Changren, a 33-year-old man from Funing, residing at No. 82 Tanziwan, Panjiawan, Zhabei, was a foreman. He lived with his elderly mother and wife in a rural house made of bamboo fences. Yesterday morning at 4:00 AM, someone suddenly called outside the door. Gao thought it was an emergency and went outside in his thin clothes. When he reached the door, men in short clothes each brandished a pistol and fired at Gao. One bullet hit the inside of his mouth, penetrating his head, while another pistol was fired into his left breast, passing through his waist. He fell to the ground and died instantly. His mother and wife were both awake and witnessed the murderers fleeing without a trace past the thatched shed. They embraced the body and wept bitterly. After properly handling the funeral arrangements yesterday afternoon, they reported the incident to the local court for examination.

Continued Trial of the Case of Detective Shot Dead by Robbers 161

Jin Baoyu, a new probationary detective No. 61 of the French Concession Police, was checking pedestrians at the intersection of Route Ghisi and Rue Belles Vues at 8:20 PM on the 6th of this month when he encountered robbers who opened fire to resist arrest, hitting him in the head and killing him instantly. A stray bullet also killed a pedestrian named Qian Achun. At that time, patrolmen No. 65 captured a robber named Wang Ziqing from Henan Province, seizing a Mauser pistol and 19 bullets. Furthermore, Jin Jiulin, an inspector of the special agency, led detectives of the same shift to No. 2, Lanfang Lane, Zhaojiabang Road in the Chinese area, and the Lin'an Hotel on Guangdong Road in the Public Concession, arresting seven accomplices, including Liu Biao, Wang Shoujing, Zheng Chang, Chuan Shunqing, Chuan, surnamed Pan, Wang Yousheng, and Wang Jusheng, seizing two pistols and seven bullets. The rest have been interrogated and detained by the Second Special Court, and the case is under investigation. All details have been reported in previous newspapers. The police have now found that the defendants were all soldiers. Wang Ziqing, Wang Yousheng, and Wang Jusheng, along with Wang Guozhong, Li Shigen, Zhang Qiang, and others who are still at large, robbed the home of Yuan A'gen at No. 13, Qingshun Lane, Route Amiral Courbet on February 16, the home of Zhou Yingshi on Zilaihuo Street, and the store opened by Shen Pinzai at No. 30, Route Amiral de Préfeln, on March 10 and May 2, dividing the loot. On the night of the incident, they attempted to rob the Zhenhe Medical Garden at No. 28, Route Sainte-Marie, but failed and turned back. They were encountered by Liang, who checked them, and they resisted arrest by opening fire, killing Detective Jin. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, the police escorted Wang and others back to the court. Judge Li Changnian and Clerk Wu Shan presided over the continued trial in the First Criminal Court. First, Police Lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the police investigation and prosecuted them for murder and robbery under Articles 282 and 346 of the Criminal Law, presenting the pistols and Mauser pistol as evidence. Wang Zijisong confessed that he was in Suzhou and was invited by Wang Guozhong, who is at large, to come to Shanghai on April 28. Because he had no money to use, his clothes were pawned. Helplessly, Wang Guozhong, Wang Yousheng, Wang Jusheng, and himself robbed a meat shop owned by a Shen, obtaining 130 yuan, of which he received nine yuan. He stated that he did not know about the other two cases and was being falsely accused. On the night of the incident, they intended to rob a soy sauce garden but failed and retreated. Wang Guozhong carried two guns, and he carried one gun, which was the Mauser pistol in question. They encountered the detective, and they opened fire. He did not fire and requested a check. After the interrogation, it was past noon, and the court announced that the trial would be adjourned to the 28th, and the defendants would remain detained in the police station.

English Book on the Sino-Japanese Question Published 162

Mr. Zhu Weijie from Nanhui, a senior student who studied in the United States, is erudite and talented, with excellent writing skills in both Chinese and Western languages. He once served as the editor of Chinese and Western newspapers in Shanghai, gaining great fame. His book "The Sino-Japanese Question" in English is fluent and well-organized, with insightful arguments and unique perspectives. It thoroughly discusses the Manchurian Incident and the Shanghai War, pinpointing the root causes and vehemently refuting the fallacies of the Japanese, leaving no room for doubt. It expresses what everyone wants to say but has not said. It is especially helpful for college students studying English. It has already been published in various Western newspapers and is now compiled into a book. It also includes a letter from Lord Lytton, Chairman of the League of Nations Investigating Commission, which further demonstrates the value of this book. It is now published and priced at 40 cents per copy. It is sold at the Biefa Foreign Firm on Nanjing Road, the Sino-American Bookstore, and the China Science Company at No. 122 Moore Road.

The Value of Revolutionary History Before the Founding of the Nation 163

"The Revolutionary History Before the Founding of the Republic of China" written by Feng Ziyou is the only reliable history that describes all the revolutionary battles before the Xinhai Revolution. All events related to the revolutionary era, including uprisings, assassinations, party organizations, newspaper publications, and fundraising, are recorded in detail and comprehensively. The full text contains more than 600,000 words with over 200 illustrations. More than 30,000 copies have been sold. The first and second volumes have long been published, with each volume reduced to 1.20 yuan. The Minzhi Bookstore, Wenming Bookstore, and Dadong Bookstore in various ports all have consignment sales. The lower volume will also be published soon.

Love Faded, Pam Renru Accused of Abandonment 165

Gao Jianying Claims Livelihood on the Brink of Ruin

Defendant Failed to Appear Yesterday

Pan Renru, residing at No. 174, Zikai Lane, Wuding Road, West Shanghai, is engaged in stock exchange business and is quite wealthy. Although he already has a family, his wife is not enough, and five years ago, he became entangled with a woman named Gao Jianying (also known as Runzhu). The woman is from Jiangsu Province, and at that time, she was seventeen years old. Her soft Wu dialect captivated Pan, and soon he built a golden house to hide her away. Over the past five years, Ms. Gao has given birth to a son and a daughter, and the green leaves have become lush, but her beauty has also diminished. Pan felt that her beauty was gradually fading, so his love also waned, and recently he has treated her like a stranger, abandoning her, causing her and her children to struggle to maintain their livelihood. Forced to do so, she hired lawyer Lin Yingqing to submit a petition to the Civil Mediation Office of the First Special District Court, requesting an order to summon Pan Renru to the court for mediation in accordance with the law, ordering him to pay 5,000 yuan for living expenses and damages, and 2,000 yuan for the education and upbringing of the children. The petition stated that Pan had maliciously abandoned her for the past two years, neglecting to provide support, causing her livelihood to be on the brink of ruin. Not only has she mortgaged everything she owns, but she is also in debt for 2,000 yuan, with no way to borrow money. Under such circumstances, the affection has been completely severed, and it is impossible to continue the relationship. Moreover, the son is four years old, and the daughter is only six months old. The future is long, and life must be sustained, debts must be repaid, and children must be raised. All of these require money. For this reason, she submitted the petition and requested the court to intervene. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Li Hu of the Civil Court opened the court to summon him, but Pan Renru did not appear, so the case could not proceed. Judge Li then ordered a second summons to Pan to appear in court and set a date for further consideration.

Accountant of Great Lai Company, Sun Liande, Accused of Embezzling Public Funds 166

Sun Liande, a local, residing at No. 248 Tangshan Road, was an accountant in the freight department of the Great Lai Steamship Company at No. 3 Guangdong Road. From December 1 of last year to May of this year, he successively embezzled public funds of 1,834 taels of silver. The director of the company, a Westerner named Bauer, found out and reported it to the Laozha Police Station. Detective Wang Rulin was dispatched to arrest Sun Liande and detain him in the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court, Criminal Court No. 1. Police Lawyer Ru Baoyi explained the case, and a Western witness named Jack, who speaks Chinese, testified that he was the bookkeeper in the Great Lai Company and that the actual amount embezzled by the defendant had not yet been determined. Therefore, he requested a postponement for further interrogation. When questioned, the defendant admitted that he had embezzled public funds due to financial difficulties. Judge Zhou Hanting verified the confession and ordered the defendant to be detained pending further investigation and interrogation next Tuesday.

Robbers Attack With Axes 167

Fang Xiaozhou's Family Suffers

At 5:20 AM yesterday (the 21st), just as dawn was breaking, five robbers suddenly broke into the home of Fang Xiaozhou, a local gang leader in Linjiagang, north of Caojiadu, West Shanghai. One robber stood guard outside, two robbers each held a sharp axe, and two robbers each held a pistol. They first fired several shots. Fang and his concubine, Ms. Yin, were sleeping soundly when they were awakened from their dreams by the sound. Fearing that they would raise an alarm and call the police, the two robbers holding the sharp axes repeatedly slashed at Fang and Ms. Yin's heads, causing them to faint in pain. The robbers then ransacked the chests and cabinets, robbing 120 yuan in silver dollars, 50 cents in small silver coins, and a pair of gold bracelets. They fled with the loot towards Zhongshan Road. Their family members took the two injured people to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. It was found that Fang had three knife wounds on his head, and Ms. Yin had two knife wounds on her head and face. They were bleeding profusely, and their injuries were quite serious. After receiving the report, the Sixth District Police Station, under the leadership of Director Zhang, ordered Inspector Xu to take Police Chief Hu Lizhong, Squad Leader Xia Pinshan, and Detectives Chen Keqing, Tang Bingxiang, Cao Chuqiao, Li Guiqing, Pei Yunzhang, and Ma Liang to immediately set out to search for the robbers. Soon after, they arrested a leading robber at No. 25, Dingkang Lane, Caojiadu Central Market, and brought him back to the district. After interrogation by Director Zhang, the robber confessed his name as Xu Aigen (nickname "Black Barbarian Dragon"), 28 years old, from Shanghai. He admitted to gathering accomplices to commit the robbery and slashing the victims. The pistols and sharp axes were taken away by his accomplices, and he did not know where they were hidden. After receiving the confession, Director Zhang further found that the robber had previously committed a robbery and was sentenced to two years in prison by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. He was released during the intense fighting in February of this year. He had long been rampant and lawless in the West Shanghai area, harming the local people, who feared and hated him. Now he dared to commit robbery and injure the victims again, which was an unforgivable crime. It was decided to detain him temporarily, pending the arrest of his accomplices, before further investigation.

Police Officers Change to Summer Uniforms 168

The Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, under Director Wen, stated that with the arrival of summer and the gradual increase in temperature, the black uniforms worn by the district and team leaders and police officers when on duty in the hot sun were particularly unsuitable for the body. Therefore, it was ordered that all district and team leaders should instruct their police officers to uniformly change to yellow summer uniforms starting from the 21st of this month (yesterday).

May 21

Special Article

Clarifying Doubts About the Non-War Construction Movement in China (Liu Zhan'en) 170

In general, people deeply cherish peace and love their country. To curb internal war and implement construction, four measures for domestic non-war construction have been proposed: (1) To establish a domestic non-war construction pact; (2) To adopt a policy of non-cooperation towards those who undermine domestic peace and participate in internal wars; (3) To reward leaders of peaceful construction; (4) To focus on peaceful construction propaganda. They are respectfully discussed with the Chinese people, hoping that all will rise up to implement them. After their publication, people from all walks of life responded positively, which shows that hating war and loving peace is a unanimous sentiment throughout the country. However, there are still some who harbor doubts about the non-war construction movement within the warlords. I respectfully submit my humble opinions to discuss with the Chinese people.

Some say, "The government loses its power and humiliates the country, and warlords divide the territory, often unfortunately leading to internal war. How should the people deal with this?" According to our current first hope, it lies in awakening the people, influencing the government, and making every effort to revitalize, strengthen ourselves, and start anew with the people. We should also influence the warlords, curb their ambitions, and serve the country. If the government disregards the fate of the nation and the survival of the people, and goes against the tide, losing its power and humiliating the country, then destruction is to be feared. We, the people, must use our entire strength to take positive and effective actions. If the warlords rely on their troops to achieve their goals, fighting endlessly, and insist on dividing the territory, then we, the people, should expose their secrets and remind the people of the country, and take appropriate measures. However, the sanctions against both parties must be resolved by non-violent means. Regardless of which party is suspected of this, the public opinion organs (which can be replaced by legally established folk professional groups before the establishment of formal national representative organs) should judge the merits and demerits and stop them. If this is not effective, and internal war unfortunately breaks out, then we, the people, must only strengthen the defenses and clear the fields, and refuse to cooperate with those who participate in internal war. The people have no military force and cannot place themselves in the midst of it. We should seek further solutions. Even if there is military force that can be used, who can guarantee that new warlords will not appear? Moreover, today's China has suffered greatly and is on the brink of destruction. No matter how we punish any disputes, we should not resort to force, which would only increase the suffering and plunge the nation and people into an irrecoverable situation.

Some say, "The cause of internal war has already been sown. If various political, social, economic, and livelihood problems are not resolved, internal war cannot be avoided." This statement is indeed very important. However, after an internal war, politics often becomes more corrupt, society becomes more unstable, the economy becomes more panicked, and livelihood becomes more difficult. It can be seen that frequent internal wars are not good, and their causes are complex and not just one. It is my opinion that we cannot talk about social transformation and national construction without first stopping internal war. The internal wars of past years have become more and more serious, and have not benefited the country or the people. It is an undeniable fact that we must first plan to prevent internal war, which is the removal of political, social, economic, livelihood, and other obstacles to progress.

Some say, "Verbal non-war, paper-based disarmament, and the initiative of a few people, what use is it?" I think that things are made by people. As long as the motive is pure and the struggle is persistent, there will be a day of success. In the past, all revolutionary undertakings were a million times more difficult when they first started. However, because of sincerity, even metal and stone can be penetrated. Therefore, with the efforts of a few people, they were able to awaken the people of the whole country. Today, we are promoting the domestic non-war movement. If we can truly make up our minds and sacrifice for peace, we will be able to influence the leading figures in the country and arouse the people to agree to participate. With this strong force, we can curb internal war. Even if we cannot see the immediate results, after a long period of time, we can eliminate the roots of future internal war and establish lasting peace. However, whether it can succeed depends entirely on whether we can make long-term efforts.

In short, today's China has experienced natural disasters such as floods and droughts, as well as the dangers of war, bandits, and thieves. The invasion of powerful enemies and the unprecedented national crisis are also just beginning. The fate of the country and the lives of the people are almost at their end. In this situation, there must be no more internal war. I hope that our compatriots will hold fast to their principles, cut through the thorns, unite as one, eliminate internal war, strive for self-reliance, and work hard to build the nation. With a spirit of selfless devotion, we must promote the domestic non-war construction movement and not stop until we achieve our goals.

Yarn and Cotton: The Yarn Market is Weak 178

The cotton yarn market is still sluggish and showing signs of weakening because demand is stagnant. Each gang is completely still, and the political disputes in Guangdong Province have not subsided, and the financial situation is still tight. Due to these various reasons, the market is in a state of sadness. Fortunately, each factory has less stock of bottom goods than before, and the standard yarn price is smaller than the current yarn, so there is no sign of a sharp drop. However, considering the overall situation, there is very little optimism. In the afternoon, some people sold short due to cheaper raw materials.

Wu Tea Shops Have Already Weighed 188

The production of new tea in Wuyuan, after days of picking and production, from the tea farmers has reached seven or eight tenths of the quota. However, the yield is lower than before. Those who work diligently and fertilize have a harvest of eight tenths of previous years. Those who are barren, old, and lack manpower have only six tenths of the harvest compared to last year. In Wunei, Wainan, and various villages, at the beginning of the new tea picking, it happened that the banditry on the border had subsided. The tea farmers rushed to pick first, and it can be heard in recent days. More than a dozen tea shops in Taibai and other places in the township have rushed to open. The tea shops in Northeast Wu have also sent people to Cao Men, Long, and Xiaogang to purchase one after another, and there should be transactions and weighing within days.

Dexing Tea is Cheap Due to Banditry 189

The quality of new tea in Dexing this year is quite good. Last month, because the Red Army in the area concentrated there, the tea farmers fled abroad, and no one picked it. The bandits and communists in the southern part of Dexing have been suppressed by the garrison troops, and the momentum is not as bad as before. Therefore, the tea farmers were reluctant to abandon their profits to the ground, and they all returned to pick when they had the opportunity. However, they did not dare to store the manufactured tea at home, and were willing to sell it at a low price. Each load only fetched 30 yuan. General profit-hungry tea merchants have been scrambling to report this and are trying to find a way to find goods.

Free Talk

Aphorisms of the Nonagenarian Ma Xiangbo

A Hasty Conclusion 193

—

My teacher, named Zotolio, was an Italian priest. He often said to me, "Chinese people lack thought. They should use their minds more." Thinking about it now, we still haven't gotten rid of this problem.

When reading foreign books, the emphasis is on thought, not recitation. The old method of reading Chinese books is the opposite. It emphasizes recitation, not seeking explanation. The ancients said, "To learn without thinking is futile; to think without learning is perilous." The method of reading foreign books is based on this principle. Our old method, on the other hand, has completely forgotten this famous saying.

Foreigners also had an old method of reading. To pass the "修才" (Bachelier) exam, Latin and Greek were required subjects. This is still the case today.

When I read foreign books, I first learned pronunciation, then phonetics. There are only 25 letters in pronunciation. It's considered done once you pronounce all 25 sounds accurately. It felt very easy. In phonetics, I first learned Romanization, then French phonetics, which was also not difficult.

Actually, studying in foreign schools might not be much better than ours. Latin and Greek are literature, poetry, prose, also literature. Our Four Books and Five Classics contain some political thought. Unfortunately, the old Chinese habit of "not seeking thorough understanding" is truly unbreakable. In the past, officials writing memorials to advise the emperor to do good deeds always spoke in a hesitant and roundabout manner, considering mawkishness amusing. After saying a few sentences, they dared not speak frankly. Logically, they should have spoken at greater length, expounded more thoroughly, and added words of encouragement. In the end, they still reached a hasty conclusion.

Ring of Clouds Over North China: Remembering a Dream Like Zhuang Zhou's Butterfly 194

—

When General Wu Ziyu entered Sichuan in the past, it was reported that "the general let his wife ride the horse along the way, while he walked. The roads in Sichuan were rugged, and his feet developed thick calluses." I said that this was an absolutely beautiful poetic scene. I imagined that the general must have composed something at the time, but there was no news from afar. Therefore, I imitated Li Changji's method of supplementing Yu Jianwu's "Returning from Kuaiji Song" and composed a seven-character poem: "Once commanded a million brave soldiers, now in decline, suffering the long march in Sichuan. Extravagance can ruin a hero's career, hardship increases the love between husband and wife. In the Chu camp, a sad song for the unreturned horse, in the Wushan clouds, the lone goose cries mournfully. With the Xiongnu not yet destroyed, where is home? Gazing at the autumn wind, the White Emperor City is distant." A playful friend saw it and said that I was originally Liu Yong, the Willow Tun Tian of Xiaofengcanyue, but now I had become Su Shi, the iron-clad bronze pipa. Wearing the clothes of an actor, I actually looked like Mei Lanfang acting as Mulan joining the army. We both laughed together. Recently, while rummaging through my travel case, I suddenly saw this draft. I thought that Fuwei is now in Beiping, and letters can be delivered by mail. I rewrote it on a piece of paper and sent it for his review. A few days later, I received a reply personally written by the general, bestowing upon me five "朵郇雲" (praises) and awarding me eight characters of monthly commentary: "Classic and sonorous, truly a masterpiece." He also gifted me three of his new books. Small gifts in exchange for great returns, precious jade in return for generosity, truly a literary緣.

The Flower-Snake-Like Long Corridor 195

—

[Random Notes from the Old Capital, Part 4]

Yanjing University held a "New Student Welcome Party" at the Summer Palace for new students and professors. I was also invited as a guest and took this opportunity to tour the Summer Palace.

I had seen many pictures of the Summer Palace in the South, so when I stood by the edge of the rippling Kunming Lake, looking at the bronze ox nearby, the Dragon King Temple of Hunan, the Stone Bridge with Thirteen Arches, and the multi-storied buildings, palaces, pavilions, towers, and lush mountains on the north shore, and the pagoda of Fragrant Hills, I didn't feel like a stranger at all. What I felt was brighter than seeing pictures, and the colors in the pictures were far less striking and charming than the real lake and mountains. So I excitedly lingered in the garden for a whole day.

On the north shore, against the mountains, is a flower-snake-like long corridor. I don't know how long this corridor is, but judging by my imagination, it must be about two miles long. The beams and rafters in the long corridor are all exquisitely painted with flowers, plants, and figures. The long corridor is surrounded by greenery and flowering trees. The season is spring, and all the flowers are in bloom. A faint fragrance lingers around you, almost making you reluctant to leave. From time to time, slender waists, brightly colored curves, and soul-stirring legs flitted through the long corridor, especially embellishing this picture-like beauty into something like you'd see in a dream.

I also went to the palaces to see the portrait of Empress Dowager Cixi and everything she enjoyed during her lifetime. I also climbed the mountain, passing through many pavilions and courtyards with Buddha statues. But in the end, I spent a lot of time in that flower-snake-like long corridor. I felt that sitting here, quietly watching the flowers and the lake, I had leisurely become a person from ancient times, and I had also entered the Grand View Garden full of ladies.

World Anecdotes 196

[Z Hai Ke]

A Strange Experience: Admiral Sir W. Goodenough, President of the Royal Geographical Society, recently told of a young man's strange experience. It was chilling to hear. One day, the young man was walking along a street in Malta when he saw a man bullying two women. He was impulsively moved by chivalry and rushed forward, punching and kicking the man to the ground. He then escorted the two women back to their home. The two women were very grateful and insisted that he stay for dinner. After dinner, he smoked a cigarette, chatted for a while, and then thanked them and left. The next day, he noticed that his cigarette case was missing. He knew that he had forgotten it in the women's house the night before. So he hurried back. But when he arrived, he found the house empty and locked. According to the neighbors, it had been empty for several years and no one lived there. He was half in doubt and half in belief, so he managed to enter the house. Sure enough, he saw that all the rooms were covered in dust and cobwebs. On a table in the dining room, however, was his cigarette case. He was stunned for a long time before fleeing in terror. Such a strange thing seems to force even those who don't believe in ghosts to consider the existence of ghosts.

Memories of Guyi Garden 197

— Zheng Yimei

Under the iron hooves of war, the prosperity of the marketplace and the grandeur of the city walls are all destroyed without a trace. How much more so the beauty of ponds, pavilions, bamboo, and trees? In the market town of Chaxi, there is a Guyi Garden, famous throughout the north and south of the Yangtze River. Tourists come in droves, enjoying the pleasures of singing and wandering. A guest from Chaxi said that when the Japanese army invaded, the garden was occupied by cavalry. The Dunren Hall and the Water Surface Pavilion were trampled upon. Even the stacked stones in front of the Chunzao Hall have mostly collapsed and fallen to the ground, no longer retaining their rugged and towering appearance. What are his feelings about the rise and fall of the past and present? My late grandfather, Jin Tinggong, was buried in Zhangjingjiao, Chaxi. Every year, we would go there to sweep his grave with simple food and paper money. I still remember that last spring, I went to Zhangjing with Jingren and made a detour to explore the secluded beauty of Guyi Garden. We passed through the Nanmu Hall,穿柳帶軒, and followed the winding path to a boat room. In the room, we brewed a pot of clear tea. My heart was broadened. Looking to the left, the peach blossoms on the bank were blooming brightly, and most of them were double-petaled, with purple patterns and red sepals, competing in fragrance and beauty. There were also white flowers mixed with ochre spots, which were even more beautiful. Even the Dragon China Road on the sea could not compare. My wife and I lingered, reluctant to leave. We thought that even in this chaotic world, this small piece of land was enough to be a paradise and escape from Qin. Who knew that after only a year, the sounds of war drums and beacon fires would destroy the famous garden? Tears flow without flowers, and birds startle the heart. I wonder when we will be able to restore the old look and revisit the place. Alas!

The Lindbergh Kidnapping Case Swindle (Part Two) 199

— Kai Xu

Initially, Peikok befriended Senator Morrow in Mexico City. At that time, Morrow was the US Ambassador to Mexico and the father of Lindbergh's wife. Brigadier General White Birch was an old acquaintance of Colonel Lindbergh. Lindbergh became famous overnight in 1927 by crossing the Atlantic Ocean. At that time, White was the commander of the US warship Memphis. When Lindbergh returned to the United States from Paris, he was a guest aboard the Memphis. Curtis initially worked in shipbuilding, but recently his business had been in decline due to the impact of the global economic depression. When the Lindbergh kidnapping case occurred, Curtis felt that there was a profit to be made. He designed a plan to have Peikok and White Birch act as intermediaries and recommend himself to Lindbergh. Lindbergh believed that all three were well-known members of society. Although he did not know Curtis very well, he did not doubt him because Peikok and White Birch were involved. Who knew that many beasts were clothed in the robes of gentlemen? Curtis's way of making a profit was not through Lindbergh's ransom but through fabricating news facts and holding them as rare commodities. Many newspapers were fooled, and it cannot be said that none of those who participated in the initial planning and encouraged the events were involved. Even a film company, believing that Curtis had discovered many secrets, agreed to give him exclusive rights in advance. Curtis fabricated facts, claiming that the kidnapping was carried out by liquor smugglers in the ocean and that there was a mysterious giant ship anchored near Virginia. If this ship could be found, Lindbergh's son would be easily recovered. Lindbergh even flew his own plane to search the coast of Virginia. The US Navy even dispatched as many as 75 warships to assist Lindbergh's search, but to no avail. Curtis's actions were absurd and ridiculous. Unexpectedly, Lindbergh's child's body was found, and the matter could no longer be kept secret. He confessed to the police. The matter is currently under investigation. It is feared that Curtis will not be able to escape the crime of fraud.

Discussion

The PEN Club and the Vegetarian Old Woman 201

— Buddha

The world-renowned literary organization "PEN Club" is holding its 10th Congress in Nanjing. The original articles of association stipulated that politics should not be discussed. However, the theme of this congress is "In what ways can PEN Club members assist the peace movement without getting involved in politics?"

What kind of statement is that? Once you assist the peace movement, you are involved in politics. How can you assist the peace movement without getting involved in politics? This is a contradiction.

However, even if the PEN Club gentlemen get involved in politics, their greatest ability is only to write a few articles, send a few peace telegrams, and unleash their brilliant theories. This is just a trick of the黔驢 (donkey from Guizhou), nothing more.

Therefore, the "pen-wielding class" is definitely not as strong as the "gun-wielding class." Facts have already told us this. Let's take two recent examples: (1) During the recent Sino-Japanese war, many members of the League of Nations, after discussing the matter, issued a resolution that Japan tore up with one hand, and the League of Nations could do nothing. (2) During the recent coup in Japan, the military faction formed a non-partisan cabinet, breaking the party cabinet. Ordinary politicians scratched their heads, unable to do anything. Therefore, it is a dream for PEN Club gentlemen to assist the peace movement without getting involved in politics.

Someone might say yes.

The vegetarian old women in our country often chant "Amitabha Buddha, bless the whole family with peace and prosperity and make the descendants flourish." Isn't this an excellent example of a peace movement that doesn't involve politics?

Also, in various countries, when wars break out, Christians often hold large peace prayer meetings. Isn't this another excellent example of a peace movement that doesn't involve politics? PEN Club gentlemen! Why don't you follow this method of peace, neutrality, and mutual non-interference?
