Simple and Easy Small Industries 205

— Nai Zheng

The following three small industries have also been successfully tested and have excellent results. The medicines and raw materials used are also cheap, the manufacturing procedures are very simple, and the finished products are also very useful. Readers may want to try them. Not only is it an interesting experiment, but it is also a way to spend your spare time.

(1) Rose Mint Body Powder (Prickly Heat Powder)

Talc Powder (French Made) 7 ounces, Boric Acid 1.5 ounces, Rose Oil (or Fragrance) 10 drops, Peppermint Oil 7 drops (only one fragrance can also be used)

Method: First, place the talc powder and boric acid together in a mortar and grind them until they are very fine. Touch them with your fingers to make sure they are soft and smooth. Then, slowly add the fragrance while stirring. If you want it to be more refined, stir well and then sieve it through a sieve. Store it in a cigarette can (a can with no smoke smell). On hot days, apply it to the skin, which will be exceptionally smooth.

(2) Sealing Wax

White Wax (not Beeswax) 4 ounces, Yellow Wax 2 ounces, Pure Rosin 4 ounces, Carmine a little (or other pigments)

Method: Place the three ingredients together in a rough bowl, melt them over a fire, and then add the coloring agents, stirring vigorously. After cooling, it will solidify. When using, heat it until it melts and pour recorder in a metal mold.

(3) Floral Water

Pure Alcohol 50 parts, Ammonia 3 parts, Essence 3 parts

Method: Mix the above three ingredients together. It is more effective than the products sold on the market. Applying this water after being bitten by an insect can stop itching and disinfect. Prickly heat can also be eliminated by this water. If the essence is peppermint, it will feel more comfortable and cool in the summer.

Artistic Ending

People Who Were Once Noble 206

— Wu

The impression that the Russian people in Shanghai gave me was not deep, perhaps because I did not pay much attention to them. However, even in the few times I came into contact with them, they had already given me considerable lessons.

A long time ago, one summer, I was at a friend's house in Tiantong'an. Looking down from the balcony, three or five ragged White Russians were begging us. My friends were quite mean. Although they wanted to give them a few coppers, they insisted on getting a considerable reward from them.

"Hey! Dance a dance and I'll give you five coppers."

So they danced desperately, sweating in the dust raised by passing cars. Tearful happiness seemed to overshadow the sorrow of exile. After a duet dance was finished, in addition to the five coppers, they also took half a cigarette I was eating.

This was the first time.

One afternoon near the Great World, I was suddenly grabbed by a barbaric old foreigner. A piece of medicine was rubbed on my clothes. I couldn't help but be stunned. Later, he gestured for me to buy his medicine, and I realized that this was also a trade. It turned out to be an oil stain remover soap. There was no way, so I had to give him a few coppers. But I had no oil stains on my clothes!

This was the second time.

In May of the year before last, many White Russians in Shanghai benefited greatly from the bus strike, and they replaced our Chinese compatriots as bus drivers. But this caused a lot of hatred among people.

Once, I was sitting on a tram on North Sichuan Road. Suddenly, the driver stopped the car and cursed "pig." I saw a White Russian driving a bus past timidly, otherwise, he might have been slapped by the tram driver. In fact, the two had no hatred, but because the White Russian had taken the bus driver's job. (It turns out that the Chinese are still clear about this point!)

This was the third time.

Another day, I was walking with someone who understood Russian.

At a tram stop, a White Russian gentleman was waiting for a tram with a child. Soon the tram stopped nearby. The foreign child pulled his father and ran to the nearby cheap carriages. But he was scolded by his father and finally turned to the first class.

Because my friend told me, I knew what the White Russian gentleman said was ...

"Low-class! Do you want to sit with the filthy workers?"

This was the fourth time.

Ah! This is the once blessed White Russian.

Required

Where Do Airplanes Come From? 207

— Ci Min

"Zhengyang was suddenly captured by the Red Bandits. The ×× division and ×× brigade were sent to encircle and suppress them. One plane from the seventh team departed from ×× to bomb them. ××When the Red Bandits flew a red flag and entered the city in formation, they dropped six or seven bombs."

Before seeing this news, I almost doubted that China had airplanes or bombs!

Currently, suppressing bandits and resisting foreign aggression are both important national programs for saving the country. Suppressing bandits is certainly important, but resisting foreign aggression cannot be ignored either. Suppressing bandits is the work of internal peace, and resisting foreign aggression is the work of external defense.

Problems such as "prioritizing external defense over internal peace" and "prioritizing internal peace over external defense" do not need to be discussed, but China has airplanes and bombs that can be used to suppress bandits. After reading the above news, we can be sure of this.

Airplanes are called the seventh team. Naturally, there are also the first, second, third ... teams. Moreover, we have no way of knowing whether the seventh team is the last team formed. However, the fact that China has at least seven teams of airplanes is ironclad. Furthermore, airplanes are called teams. We also have no way of knowing how many airplanes there are in each team. However, everyone believes that each team has more than one or two.

Alas! Recalling when our troops were fighting bravely against the Japanese in Shanghai, I don't know where China's many airplanes went. Where did they hide!

Airplanes are not needed for resisting foreign aggression, but they must be used for suppressing bandits. Does this make sense?

An army can say that mountains and rivers are obstacles and it is inconvenient to transfer them, but are airplanes also afraid of mountains and rivers as obstacles?

All of these, all of these, cannot help but raise many questions.

A University Student's Loss 208

— Yan Ye

In the war zone of Shanghai, several universities have tragically suffered from ruthless artillery fire, leaving them shattered and dilapidated. These venerable institutions of learning have become mere ruins. The universities themselves have undoubtedly suffered, and naturally, their students cannot escape losses either.

One university student, whose most heart-wrenching loss this time wasn't his books or anything of that nature, but rather twenty-one Western suits, six overcoats, and seven pairs of leather shoes. When he returned home for the winter break, he took nothing with him except the clothes on his back. Little did he expect that these prized possessions, separated from him for only a few days, would be gone forever.

The total value of his loss is estimated at around fifteen hundred gold dollars, as each suit averaged about fifty yuan, each overcoat about seventy yuan, and each pair of shoes about twenty yuan.

To a university student who doesn't forget romance while studying, what does a mere fifteen hundred gold dollars worth of clothing mean? As I write this, I can't help but laugh at my own busybodying.

Movies

Street Hero 209

Chaplin's famous work "Street Hero" (The Big Adventure), which has been playing at the Paris Grand Theatre for several consecutive days, has been extremely well-received by all walks of life in Shanghai. This is because the play is rich in comedic elements, full of interest, and every move of Chaplin is a masterpiece of heartfelt skill. For example, if you want to see an expression of fear and embarrassment, we only need to close our eyes and think, and we will find it difficult to restrain ourselves from laughing. Moreover, seeing it on the screen, it is no wonder that laughter and applause continue incessantly. Today and tomorrow are the last two days, and those who want to see Chaplin's demeanor should reserve seats early, otherwise, it is inevitable to miss out.

Cathay Screens "Emma's History of Hatred" The comedic queen Marie Dressler, who previously starred in films such as "Min and Bill" and "Reducing", has been praised by all. In 1931, she was selected as the Queen of Hollywood. Now, she is starring in another film, originally titled EMMA, translated as "Emma's History of Hatred." Not only is the humor witty and clever, but its sorrowful aspects can also admonish the world and encourage customs. It is indeed a rare masterpiece since the advent of film, and Dressler's reputation has become even higher because of this film. It is heard that the Cathay Grand Theatre on Avenue Joffre has begun screening this film today (Sunday).

"The Truth Revealed" and "Case Within a Case" Shanghai once screened a famous detective film called "The Truth Revealed," originally called Alibi. Today, the "Case Within a Case" opening at the Carlton is also called Alibi, and it also narrates a bizarre and mysterious detective story. Initially, a wealthy widow is murdered, and then a duke, who is in love with the wealthy widow, is suddenly murdered and killed. Suspicions arise, and no one knows who the murderer is. Later, after a famous French detective investigates in various ways, the truth finally comes to light. It turns out that the murderer is a seemingly kind-hearted but ruthless doctor that no one would have guessed. The plot is tense, intriguing, and even more exciting than "The Truth Revealed."
